# Frequently Asked Questions

### About the company: what is OpenWeather?

OpenWeather (headquartered in London) is a team of IT-intellectuals that create pivotal products for business using climate data. For each point on the globe, OpenWeather provides hyperlocal minutely forecast, historical data, current state, and from short-term to annual forecasted weather data. All data is available via [industry standard APIs](/api.md).

OpenWeather Ltd. has more than 9 million users including Fortune 500 companies and thousands of other businesses globally.

### How to get an API key?

To use OpenWeather services, you first need to create an OpenWeather account. Once your account is created and your email address is verified, you will receive your personal API key (APPID), which is required to access our APIs and other OpenWeather services. 
Getting started is easy:

1. [Sign up](https://home.openweathermap.org/users/sign_up) for an OpenWeather account to get an API key (APPID) on [your account page](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys)
2. Verify your email address using the confirmation email we sent you. If you do not receive it, you can resend the verification email from your profile settings one hour after registration
3. After verification, check your Inbox again to find our welcome email that contains your API key and important information

Congratulations! Now you have a Free [OpenWeather account](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) and can start using our services. We also recommend reading our [API documentation](/api.md) to learn how to integrate and use our APIs effectively.

### What products and types of data can I request?

For each point on the globe, OpenWeather provides hyperlocal minutely forecast, historical data, current state, and from short-term to annual and forecasted weather data. All data is available via [industry standard APIs](/api.md).

[One Call API by call](/api/one-call-4.md):

Make just one API call and get all your essential weather data for a specific location with One Call API 4.0.

- Current weather
- 1-minute forecast for 1 hour
- Hourly forecast for 48 hours
- Daily forecast for 8 days
- National weather alerts
- Weather data for 47+ years history archive and 4 days ahead forecast by timestamp
- Daily aggregated weather data for 47+ years historical archive and 1,5 year forecast ahead
- Weather overview with a human-readable weather summary for today and tomorrow's forecast, utilizing OpenWeather AI technologies
- AI Weather Assistant for retrieving weather data and weather-related advice in a human-readable and friendly format

For more functionality, please consider our generous professional subscriptions.

Professional collections:

[Current Weather and Forecasts Collection](/api.md#current)

How to get:

- [APIs](/api.md) (you can request data for geographic coordinates, ZIP codes, city name, city ID, number of cities)
- [Bulk Download](/bulk.md) (download already collected and regularly updated data for a list of global locations; available for premium subscriptions)

[Historical Weather Collection](/api.md?filter=historical#collections)

How to get:

- On-the-fly bulks for customised lists of coordinates
- [Marketplace](https://home.openweathermap.org/marketplace) of prepared data sets (coordinates, cities, zip codes) - History Bulk (47+ years back), History Forecast Bulk (from 7 Oct 2017)
- APIs to a timestamp / a period (subscriptions with different limits on calls and depth of archive)

[Specialised products:](/full-price.md#alerts)

- [Solar Irradiance API](/api/solar-irradiance.md)
- [Solar Panels Energy Prediction](/api/solar-panels-and-energy-prediction-2.md)
- [Global Weather Alerts](/api/push-weather-alerts.md)
- [Road Risk API](/api/road-risk.md)
- [Global Precipitation Maps - Forecast and historical data](/api/global-precipitation-map-forecast.md)
- [Weather Maps 2.0 with 1-hour step](/api/weather-map-1h.md)

Detailed information about all our products can be found on the [Pricing page](/full-price.md).

### Do I need to activate my API key?

Your API key will be activated automatically, up to 2 hours after your successful registration. We invite you to read the [API documentation](/api.md) that explains how to use our APIs.

### How can I use an API key in API calls?

To authorise a request from you and process it, we require you to use your unique API key in each API call.

In order to do this, add your API key as an *appid* parameter to the GET request, like in the following example:

`api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?id=524901&appid=YOUR_API_KEY`

Just use your API key instead of “YOUR_API_KEY” with your personal API key, it can be found in your personal account on the [“API keys” page](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys). You can also create additional API keys there.

### Where can I find my API key(s) and generate additional ones?

Your API key can be found in your personal account on the [“API keys” page](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys). You can always create additional API keys there.

### How many keys can I create?

You can create as many keys as you like.  Any API key associated with your account can be used with all subscribed products. API call limits are applied at the account level, not per API key. Usage from all API keys associated with your account is combined and counted toward the same account limits. When choosing a subscription plan, make sure to consider the total expected API usage across all your API keys and subscribed products, as subscription plans have different daily and per-minute API call limits.

More information about subscription limits can be found on the [Pricing page](/full-price.md).

### How to delete an API key?

You can delete unnecessary API keys but please note that your account with us should have at least 1 API key at any time.

To find your API key, go to your personal account and click the [“API keys” tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys)

When you have more than 1 registered API key, there will be an option to delete an API key.

### How often is the weather data updated?

The frequency of weather data updates depends on your subscription. Please find more information on our [“Detailed pricing” page](/full-price.md#current), the “Weather API data update” part.

### What should I do if I subscribed before creating an account?

If you subscribed before creating an OpenWeather account, an account was automatically created using the email address you provided during the subscription process.

To access your account, you need to reset your password:

1. Click [“Sign in”](https://home.openweathermap.org/users/sign_in) in the top-right corner of the website
2. Click on "Select Lost your password? Click here to recover"
3. Follow the instructions sent to your email address

### What should I do if I didn't receive the confirmation email?

If you haven't received the confirmation email, try the following:

1. Check your **Spam** or **Junk** folder. If you find the email there, mark it as **Not Spam** to ensure future emails from OpenWeather are delivered to your Inbox
2. Wait at least **1 hour** after registration. You can then resend the verification email from your account settings: [https://home.openweathermap.org/home](https://home.openweathermap.org/home)
3. If you still don't receive the email, you can send another verification email **3 hours after your previous resend request**

If you still haven't received the verification email after following these steps, please contact us at [**info@openweathermap.org**](mailto:info@openweathermap.org) for assistance.

### What is One Call API 4.0? What does this product include?

[One Call API 4.0](/api/one-call-4.md) is a unified weather intelligence API designed to give developers, digital products, and enterprise teams access to current weather, short-term forecasts, long-range daily outlooks, historical weather records, and official weather alerts through a single integration.

One Call API 4.0 simplifies weather data access by consolidating multiple temporal layers of weather information into one coherent API product. With a single API key and a standard request model based on geographic coordinates, teams can access:

- Current weather conditions
- Minute-by-minute forecast data for the next 60 minutes
- 15-minute forecast data for the next 48 hours
- Hourly weather timelines spanning 47 years of history and 48 hours of forecast
- Daily weather timelines spanning 47 years of history and up to 1.5 years ahead
- Detailed weather alert information from national agencies

This combination helps businesses reduce integration complexity, shorten development time, and create richer weather-aware experiences across consumer, commercial, and industrial use cases.

One Call API 4.0 is included to the ["Pay as you call" subscription type](/faq.md#payasyoucall). Please note, that you do not need to subscribe to any other OpenWeather subscription plans to get access to the One Call API 4.0. If you are ready to subscribe to the One Call API 4.0, please refer to the [Pricing page](/price.md).

### How much does subscription on the One Call API 4.0 cost?

Subscription on the One Call API 4.0 allows you to pay only for the number of API calls made to this product. 1,000 API calls per day are included for free. Our system sums up the number of calls that were in excess of the free limit (1,000 calls per day). You will be automatically charged at the end of your subscription months.

If you unsubscribe before the end of your subscription month, then you will be charged at the time of unsubscribing.

Please refer to the [Pricing page](/price.md) to find information about actual price for calls to One Call API 4.0.

### How to start use the One Call 4.0?

First, please create your account by [signing up](https://openweathermap.org/home/sign_up) with your email, if haven't OpenWeather account yet, and find API keys in the [‘API keys’ tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys).

Second, on the [Pricing page](/full-price.md#onecall), click 'Subscribe' button in the "One Call API 4.0" section. Fill out a short billing form and complete your subscription. Please pay attention, that you do not need to sign up any other subscriptions to get access to the One Call API 4.0.

Congratulations! Now you can start using the [One Call API 4.0](/api/one-call-4.md). Please note that the limit of 2,000 API calls per day is set by default. You can always change this limit at the ["Billing plan" tab](/subscriptions.md) in your Personal account.

Before you subscribe to our service, please read [Terms and conditions of sale](https://), [Privacy policy](http://openweather.co.uk/privacy-policy), and [Websites terms and conditions of use](https://openweather.co.uk/api/files/file/Openweather_website_terms_and_conditions_of_use.pdf).

Third, make an API call according [One Call API 4.0](/api/one-call-4.md) documentation.

### What is Professional API collections?

The Professional API collections include several products in each subscription plan. Unlike the ["Pay as you Call" subscription type](/faq.md#payasyoucall), professional subscriptions have a fix price per month and API call limits (number of API calls per minute and number of API calls per month).

The Professional API collections contain access to weather historical data, current and various forecasts. These collections also allow users to request weather maps and get weather data not only via API, but with other instruments.

### I want to start using of the professional subscriptions. Where do I begin?

It is easy and takes a couple of steps.

First, please create your account by [signing up](/home/sign_up.md) with your email and find API keys in the [‘API keys’ tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys).

On the [Pricing page](/full-price.md#current), choose a proper subscription, click 'Subscribe'. Fill out a short billing form, check the details and complete your subscription. You can also subscribe from the settings page in the [‘Billing plans’ section](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions).

For bank transfer or any other individual conditions, please contact [our team](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

Before you subscribe to our service, please read [Terms and conditions of sale](https://openweather.co.uk/api/files/file/OpenWeather_T%26C_of_sale.pdf), [Privacy policy](http://openweather.co.uk/privacy-policy), and [Websites terms and conditions of use](https://openweather.co.uk/api/files/file/Openweather_website_terms_and_conditions_of_use.pdf).

### What is the depth of historical weather data that you provide?

We offer [historical weather data](/api.md?filter=historical#collections) for any location for 47+ years back (since 1st January 1979). You can find more information about specific products in the Historical Weather Collection section of our [“Pricing” page](/price.md#history).

### Do professional subscription plans provide access to historical data?

The [Historical Weather Collection](/api.md?filter=historical#collections) provides access to 47+ years of historical data - please see our [Pricing page](/full-price.md#history).

### Can I download the missed historical data?

At OpenWeather, we understand the importance of reliable access to weather data for your operations. To ensure data integrity and availability, our systems are designed to store historical weather data for a specified period. Exclusively for Enterprise tariff users, we provide the opportunity to download missed data free of charge by contacting our support team at [info@openweathermap.org](mailto:info@openweathermap.org). We recommend regularly downloading and backing up your data to avoid any potential disruptions.

For personalised assistance with data recovery, please feel free to get in touch [with us](mailto:info@openweathermap.org).

### How do I choose the right subscription?

The structure of our [Pricing](/full-price.md) is quite simple.

The [Current Weather and Forecasts Collection](/price.md) provides access to a range of products such as current weather, forecasts, short-term historical data, weather maps and other products.

We provide a completely Free plan. If its functionality is not enough for the size of your applications, we suggest a variety of subscriptions with ability to call APIs more intensively, higher availability of service (up to 99.9%) and premium level of support.

The [Historical Weather Collection](/price.md#history) provides access to up 47+ years’ worth of detailed historical weather data for any location. You can request data via APIs [or by a one-time export of historical data](https://home.openweathermap.org/marketplace) for a list of locations.

If you need an advice on choosing the correct subscription, please contact [our team](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) for assistance.

### Can I subscribe for more than one month?

Yes, we support the annual/biannual and other options. Please contact [our team](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) for details.

### I need more information about the API call limits of my professional subscription.

The number of API calls you are allowed to make depends on [the subscription](/price.md) you choose.

For any professional subscription you should to maintain your usage below **both** per-minute and per-month limits.

### What happens if I exceed the API calls limit of my professional subscription?

**For Free plan**

We will notify you and ask you to either migrate to a subscription plan that meets your needs or reduce a number of API calls accordingly. We expect you to take one or another action to avoid suspending of your account.

**For users with paid plans**

We always contact you to find a suitable solution for you.

### How will I be charged for my subscription for recurring monthly payments?

**For monthly recurring payments**

You will be charged a fixed monthly fee based on the subscription plan you select on the [“Pricing” page](/full-price.md). In this case, the fee will be taken from your payment card. In your first month, you will be charged immediately after subscribing. The next payment will be a month later, and so on. The fee is subject to change, but we always notify you beforehand.

You can subscribe [here](/price.md).

**For long-term subscriptions via manual invoicing**

In case of manual invoicing, the payment process is discussed personally with each customer.

If you want to set up a long-term subscription, please contact our [support team](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

### Can you customise an API?

We have a rich experience of cooperation with corporate customers providing them with an individual approach and personalised service. We are ready to discuss and estimate any customisations. It is possible for the Enterprise license holders. For more details, please [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

### How to unsubscribe from your service?

If you would like to unsubscribe, please [log in to your account](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) on our website, then use the “Unsubscribe” button opposite your active plan in your personal account. After cancellation your subscription will still remain active until the end of the month for which you have paid.

If you pay by manual invoicing and would like to cancel your subscription, please contact [our support team](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

### What is "Pay as you call" subscription type? What does this subscription include?

The "Pay as you call" subscription type is a subscription type that allows you to pay only for the number of API calls made to the product. This subscription type is applicable to [One Call API 4.0](/api/one-call-4.md) and [Solar Irradiance API](/api/solar-irradiance.md) products. Please pay attention that each of the products has separate "pay as you call" subscription and price.

If you are ready to subscribe to the "Pay as you call" subscription type, please refer to the [Pricing page](/price.md).

### I want to start using "Pay as you call" subscription type. Where do I begin?

Please pay attention that "Pay as you call" subscription type is applicable to [One Call API 4.0](/api/one-call-4.md) and [Solar Irradiance API](/api/solar-irradiance.md) products.

Start using "Pay as you call" subscriptionis easy and takes a couple of steps.

First, please create your account by [signing up](/home/sign_up.md) with your email and find API keys in the [‘API keys’ tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys).

On the [Pricing page](/full-price.md#onecall), find desired product, click 'Subscribe' button. Fill out a short billing form and complete your subscription. Please pay attention, that you do not need to sign up any other subscriptions to get access to the "Pay as you call" subscription.

Congratulations! Now you can start using the "Pay as you call" subscription. Please note that the limit of API calls per day is set by default. You can always change this limit at the ["Billing plan" tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) in your Personal account.

Before you subscribe to our service, please read [Terms and conditions of sale](https://openweather.co.uk/api/files/file/OpenWeather_T%26C_of_sale.pdf), [Privacy policy](http://openweather.co.uk/privacy-policy), and [Websites terms and conditions of use](https://openweather.co.uk/api/files/file/Openweather_website_terms_and_conditions_of_use.pdf).

### Where can I find how much calls I make?

You can find the statistics of your calls usage on the "View usage statistics" button at the ["Billing plan" tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) in your Personal account.

### How and when I will be charged for the calls?

Our system sums up the number of calls that were made or made in excess of the free limit (for products where free limit is available). You will be automatically charged at the end of your subscription months.

If you unsubscribe before the end of your subscription month, then you will be charged at the time of unsubscribing.

### I'm worried that I might accidentally make too many calls and be charged for them. How can I limit API calls?

When you subscribe to a Pay as you Call plan, a default daily API call limit is automatically assigned for each subscribed product.

To change this limit:

1. Sign in to your OpenWeather account.
2. Open the ["Billing plans" tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) in your Personal account.
3. Update the daily API call limit for the desired product.

Please refer to the screenshot below for an example:

![limits default](/payload/api/media/file/limits_default.png)

Please note:

- Daily API call limits are reset every day between 00:00 and 00:05 UTC.
- If your account has already been blocked after reaching the previous daily limit, increasing the limit will not immediately remove the block.
- The new daily limit will take effect after the next daily reset, when the block is automatically lifted.

If you need the block removed before the next daily reset, please contact us at [info@openweathermap.org](mailto:info@openweathermap.org).

### I received the "429" error in API response. Why?

You can recieve "429" error in only one case - if you make the number of calls that exceeds the set limit of calls per day or per month.

Please note that the limit of API calls per day is set by default. You can always change this limit on the ["Billing plans" tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions). Please see the screen below:

![limits default](/payload/api/media/file/limits_default.png)

### Which payment methods we accept?

We accept most major credit and debit cards, as well as digital wallets, including Visa, Mastercard, UnionPay, American Express, Apple Pay, Google Pay, Link by Stripe, WeChat Pay, Alipay+, and Revolut Pay.

Bank transfers are also available for premium accounts. You can select your preferred payment method during the subscription process.

### Payments we do not accept

We do not accept cash or check payments.

### Is my payment secure?

All transactions made on the OpenWeather website are secure. We use HTTPS secure protocol over the website. We do not collect, store or process any of your payment details.

### Where is my invoice?

You can find invoices and transaction history in the ['Payments' section](https://home.openweathermap.org/payments) of your settings.

Note that you need to add your company information in the ['Invoice info' tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/invoice_info) in your personal account.

For bank transfer payments, our support team send invoices directly to your email. You can always [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) if you have any questions.

### What happens after I pay for a subscription?

After receiving your payment, your API key will get activated and you will receive a confirmation email with API endpoints and guides.

### How can I upgrade or downgrade my subscription plan?

**Please note that you can upgrade or downgrade only one of the **[**professional subscriptions**](/price.md#current)**.**

**If you pay by monthly recurring payments (via payment card):**

Please [log in to your account](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) on our website, then use the “Subscribe” button underneath the desired plan in your personal account.

You will be charged immediately when you upgrade or downgrade your subscription. Note, that for your automatic subscription there is no any recalculation of payment that has already been done. To avoid double payment, we recommend you to change your subscription plan at the end of the month for which you have paid.

For example, if you have a Startup subscription and your billing payment date is the 15th day of each month, we would recommend to upgrade/downgrade your subscription on the 14th.

**If you pay by manual invoice**

You can сhange your subscription plan by [contacting us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

### How can I change my payment details?

To change your credit card details for your OpenWeather account, you have two options depending on your payment method:

1. If you are using a credit card directly, please sign in to your account and visit this link to update your payment card details: [this link](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions/customer_portal).
2. If you have used PayPal, you can update your payment details through your registered PayPal account using: [this link](https://www.paypal.com/uk/cshelp/article/how-do-i-add-my-bank-account-to-my-paypal-account-help183). If you paid using a guest PayPal account, you should resubscribe with your API key on the last day of your current subscription to avoid any interruptions or duplicate charges by following: [this link](/price_subscribe.md).

If you prefer to subscribe directly using your credit card (instead of PayPal), you will need to wait until your current subscription ends before resubscribing again.

If you still have any questions please [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions)for assistance and specify your account email.

### How can I change information represented on the invoice (company info, address, etc.)?

Please sign in and use this link: [https://home.openweathermap.org/invoice_info](https://home.openweathermap.org/invoice_info).

### What happens if my payment fails?

If you have subscribed via our website and are paying for your monthly subscription automatically, our system will make several attempts (up to 4) to charge your payment card. These attempts will happen with a minimum of 1-day difference between each charging attempt.

In case we are not able to charge you after the final attempt, your subscription will be cancelled automatically, and your account will be suspended.

You have to [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) for help if your account was suspended.

### Where can I change my password?

Your password can be changed in the [“My profile/User settings”](https://home.openweathermap.org/home) section of our website.

### How can I reset my password?

You can reset your password on the [“Sign in”](https://home.openweathermap.org/users/sign_in) page of our website by following the link after the question “Lost your password?” or by clicking "Change password" button at the ["User settings"](https://home.openweathermap.org/home) chapter at the "My profile" section of "Personal account" page.

### Can I change my account email?

Yes, we can change your account email. Please [send us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) you current email, new email, and your API key.

### Can I change the country of my account?

Yes, we can change your country. Please [send us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) the country you need to change to.

### I have exceed my subscription limits. How long my account will be suspended?

Our blocking system suspends your account for a couple of hours to several days **randomly**. If you want to be unlocked immediately, please [subscribe](/price.md) to our paid subscriptions.

### I want to know how many API calls I do?

For professional subscriptions we do not provide statistics on how many calls the user is making to our APIs. The best way to find how many calls you are making is to add counters on your end, so it could tell you the exact amount of how many times you have sent your request to the API.

For "Pay as you call" subscription plan you can find the statistics of calls usage on the "View usage statistics" button at the ["Billing plan" tab](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions) in your Personal account.

### I want to delete my account; how should I do it?

You can always delete your account in the [“My profile/Privacy centre”](https://home.openweathermap.org/privacy/notifications) section of your settings.

Please note:

- Before deleting your account, you'll need to cancel any active paid subscriptions
- Account deletion is permanent and cannot be undone
- Once your account is deleted, all associated data will be permanently removed from our system

### How can I change my account type from personal to business?

To change your account type from personal to business, you must first cancel your current subscription.

Follow these steps:

1. Sign in to your OpenWeather account
2. Go to the Subscriptions page: [https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions)
3. Cancel your current subscription and confirm the cancellation

After your subscription has been cancelled, contact us at [info@openweathermap.org](mailto:info@openweathermap.org), and we will assist you with updating your account type.

Please note: Changing your account type is only possible after the current subscription has been canceled.

### How can I change the VAT ID for my account?

To update the VAT ID associated with your account, you must first cancel your current subscription.

Follow these steps:

1. Sign in to your OpenWeather account.
2. Go to the Subscriptions page: [https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions)
3. Cancel your current subscription and confirm the cancellation.

After your subscription has been cancelled, contact us at [info@openweathermap.org](mailto:info@openweathermap.org). We will update the VAT ID associated with your account, after which you can subscribe again using the updated billing information.

Please note: Your current subscription must be cancelled before we can update the VAT ID associated with your account.

### Why is my account locked?

Your account can be temporarily locked after 5 unsuccessful login attempts to help protect it from unauthorised access.

Here's what you need to know:

- The account remains locked for 1 hour.
- During the lockout period, you cannot sign in or reset your password.
- Once the lockout period ends, you will have 5 new login attempts

### How to ensure that I give the attribution to OpenWeather correctly?

For the plans between Free and Professional, the attribution requirement is obligatory. When it is required by your license you should place the following information in the visible part of your solution:

- ‘Weather data provided by OpenWeather’
- Hyperlink to our website [https://openweathermap.org/](/index.md)
- OpenWeather logo. We provide a library of different styles to match your application design. You can [**download them here**](https://openweathermap.org/storage/app/media/logo_files.zip).

If you have any doubts about your specific scenario, please reach out to our [support team](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) and we will be glad to advise.

### What models do you use?

OpenWeather provides accurate weather data by drawing on trusted sources such as weather stations, satellites, radar systems, and advanced models like GFS, ECMWF, and its own OWHL™️. These partnerships with the UK Met Office and other national meteorological agencies boost reliability, with updates released every 10 minutes to ensure precision. Remarkably, the OWHL™️ model reports less than 1% of temperature predictions deviating by more than 5°C. Widely recognised as a leading provider of short-term forecasts, OpenWeather acknowledges that accuracy diminishes over longer periods due to atmospheric complexity. Thus, while short-term forecasts remain highly reliable, it is prudent to view predictions beyond a week with a degree of caution.

Continuously refining its models using real-time data, OpenWeather delivers reliable forecasts worldwide, covering both remote and densely populated areas. It also offers minute-by-minute precipitation data and hyperlocal insights, establishing itself as a trusted choice for businesses across the globe. You can find out more about OpenWeather model [here](https://openweather.co.uk/technology).

### I have a weather station. Can I connect my station with your system?

If you also believe in the significance of climate data in tackling climate and healthcare challenges and would like to contribute to our initiatives, then we invite you to connect your automated weather station to our platform. The accuracy of weather data benefits from enthusiasts from all over the world and we reward these contributions with our Startup plan.

To contribure your data to our system, please use the [Weather station API](/stations.md). To get access to the Startup plan, please [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

### What are the minimum/maximum temperature fields in the Current Weather API and Forecast Weather API?

In the [Current Weather API](/current.md) and [Hourly Forecast API](/api/hourly-forecast.md):

As it is a current weather data that reflect weather conditions only for the current moment, we add optional statistical parameters the `temp_min` and `temp_max` fields to show dispersion of temperature at this current moment. This is the minimum/maximum currently observed temperature or forecast temperature (within large megalopolises and urban areas).

In the [16-Day Forecast API](/forecast16.md) and [30-Day Forecast](/api/forecast30.md)

The `list.temp.min` and `list.temp.max` fields are minimum/maximum daily temperature, and show the minimum and maximum temperatures in the day.

### Which time format and timezone are used?

OpenWeather uses Unix time and the UTC/GMT time zone for all API calls, including current weather, forecast and historical weather data. The `timezone_offset` parameter shows the shift in seconds from UTC. In the [One Call API 4.0 response](/api/one-call-4.md), there is also a timezone parameter that shows the time zone name for the requested location.

### Why I do not see some parameters in the API response?

If you do not see some of the parameters in your API response, it means that these weather phenomena just have not happened for the selected location at the time of measurement. Only actually measured or calculated data is displayed in an API response.

### What is the format of the API response?

The JSON format is used by default. To get data in the XML or HTML format, just use “xml” or “html” for the `mode` parameter. The HTML format is available for [Current Weather API](/current.md) only. For the [One Call API 4.0](/api/one-call-4.md), data is only available in the JSON format. If the `mode` parameter is omitted, the format is JSON by default.

Examples of API calls:

- JSON: `api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?q=London&{YOUR_API_KEY}`
- XML: `api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?q=London&mode=xml&{YOUR_API_KEY}`
- HTML: `api.openweathermap.org/data/2.5/weather?q=London&mode=html&{YOUR_API_KEY}`

### What are the weather condition codes and icons?

A list of weather condition codes with icons (range of thunderstorm, drizzle, rain, snow, clouds, atmosphere including extreme conditions such as tornado or hurricane) can be found [here](/weather-conditions.md#How-to-get-icon-URL).

You are free to use these icons in your own solutions.

### How can I specify locations in API calls?

Requesting API calls by geographical coordinates is the most accurate way to specify any location. If you need to convert city names and zip-codes to geo coordinates and the other way around automatically, please use our [Geocoding API](/api/geocoding-api.md).

However, some of our APIs support in-built geocoding, which allows users to call weather data by city name, city ID and Zip-code. If the chosen API supports built-in geocoding, then you will find the "Buil-it geocoding" section in the API documentation.

We support over 200,000 cities worldwide and our data is available for any coordinates around the globe. However, we don't recommend using large locations or countries as it will not be weather data for a large location (aggregated data or averages), but weather data for a central point of the territory.

### Where can I find a list of City IDs?

For current and forecast products (Current API, Hourly Forecast API, Daily Forecast for 16 days, Climatic forecast for 30 days, 5 day/3 hour forecast data) can be downloaded [here](http://bulk.openweathermap.org/sample/).

Please note that you can also make requests to our APIs by using coordinates, ZIP codes, etc. Please refer to documentation of specific API to see all available options.

### How to determine polar day and polar night using sunset and sunrise time?

Polar day and polar night are natural phenomenons which occur when day and night respectively lasts more than 24 hours and observed for the northernmost and southernmost regions of Earth. During polar day and polar night time of sunset and sunrise are coincide.

So, if sunset and sunrise time for specified location are the same:

- Polar day will be observed for locations in North hemisphere from March till September and for locations in South hemisphere from September till March
- Polar night will be observed for locations in North hemisphere from September till March and for locations in South hemisphere from March till September

### What X, Y tile coordinate numbers are possible for given zoom level in the OpenWeather tiled map?

The following table provides an indication of zoom levels, possible X, Y tile coordinate numbers, the quantity of tiles at each zoom level, and the scale of each level.

| Zoom level | Possible X, Y tile coordinate number (only integers are available) | Quantity of tiles | Examples of area to represent |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 0 | 1 | 1 | whole world |
| 1 | 0-1 | 4 | one quarter of the world |
| 2 | 0-3 | 16 | subcontinental area |
| 3 | 0-7 | 64 | largest country |
| 4 | 0-15 | 256 | largest country |
| 5 | 0-31 | 1024 | large African country |
| 6 | 0-63 | 4,096 | large European country |
| 7 | 0-127 | 16,384 | small country, US state |
| 8 | 0-255 | 65,536 | wide area, large metropolitan area |
| 9 | 0-511 | 262,144 | wide area, metropolitan area |

### What is the correlation between solar irradiance and solar irradiation?

The basic definitions of solar power sector are solar irradiation and solar irradiance and are often used interchangeably. However, they are not a synonyms:

**Solar irradiation** is the total energy received by a surface of the Earth per unit area over a given period of time. It is the amount of radiation (also known as shortwave radiation) passing through a horizontal plane. Solar irradiance is measured in Wh/m2.

**Solar irradiance** is the surface power density received by a surface of the Earth. Solar irradiance is measured in W/m2.

To convert irradiance to irradiation please use the formula below:

**Energy(Wh/m****2****) = Power(W/m****2****) * TimeInterval(h)**

where energy is a solar irradiation; power is a solar irradiance.

For energy data values for 1 h period of TimeInterval = 1

For energy data values for 15 min period of TimeInterval = 0.25

For more details about what technologies, algorithms, etc. are behind the Solar Irradiance & Energy Prediction service can be found [here](/api/solar-radiation/behind-solar-radiation-api.md).

### Wind cardinal and degree directions correlation

Wind direction is reported as an orientation from where the wind is blowing. The directions of the wind is determined at the geographical system of coordinates and could be represented in degrees and cardinals terms. wind direction in degrees -azimuth degrees, i.e., in a numerical measure that moves around the Rose of the Winds in a clockwise circle from 0 degrees (N) to 360 degrees (N).Wind direction in cardinals - direction based on are the four main compass directions: north, south, east, and west. Relative to north, the directions east, south, and west are at 90 degree intervals in the clockwise direction.
Please find below the table with correlations between cardinal and degree wind directions:

| Cardinal Direction | Degree Direction | ![wind cardinal direction](/payload/api/media/file/wind-cardinal-direction.png) |
| --- | --- | --- |
| N | 348.75-11.25 |  |
| NNE | 11.25-33.75 |  |
| NE | 33.75-56.25 |  |
| ENE | 56.25-78.75 |  |
| E | 78.75-101.25 |  |
| ESE | 101.25-123.75 |  |
| SE | 123.75-146.25 |  |
| SSE | 146.25-168.75 |  |
| S | 168.75-191.25 |  |
| SSW | 191.25-213.75 |  |
| SW | 213.75-236.25 |  |
| WSW | 236.25-258.75 |  |
| W | 258.75-281.25 |  |
| WNW | 281.25-303.75 |  |
| NW | 303.75-326.25 |  |
| NNW | 326.25-348.75 |  |

### API calls return an error 400000

You can get the 400000 error when you request data for a period not covered by your subscription. Access to specific time ranges in each product depends on your subscription level. You can check the allowed data range for each subscription and product on the [Pricing page](/price.md). If you need access to data beyond the permitted range, consider upgrading your plan.

### API calls return an error 401

You can get the error 401 in the following cases:

- You did not specify your [API key](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys) in API request.
- Your API key is not activated yet. Within the next couple of hours, it will be activated and ready to use.
- You are using wrong API key in API request. Please, check your right API key in [personal account](https://home.openweathermap.org/api_keys).
- You are using a Free subscription and try requesting data available in other subscriptions . For example, [16 days/daily forecast API](/forecast16.md), [any historical weather data](/price.md#history), [Weather maps 2.0](/api/weather-map-2.md), etc). Please, check your subscription in your [personal account](https://home.openweathermap.org/).

### API calls return an error 404

You can get this error when you specified the wrong city name, ZIP-code or city ID. For your reference, this list contains City name, City ID, Geographical coordinates of the city (lon, lat), Zoom, etc.

You can also get the error 404 if the format of your API request is incorrect. In this case, please review it and check for any mistakes. To see examples of correct API requests, please visit the [Documentation](/api.md) of a specific API and read the examples of API calls there.

### API calls return an error 429

You can recieve this error in the following cases:

- If you have a Free plan of Professional subscriptions and make more than 60 API calls per minute (surpassing the limit of your subscription). To avoid this situation, please consider upgrading to a [subscription plan](/full-price.md#current) that meets your needs or reduce the number of API calls in accordance with the limits.

### API calls return errors 500, 502, 503 or 504

In case you receive one of the following errors 500, 502, 503 or 504 please [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions) for assistance. Please enclose an example of your API request that receives this error into your email to let us analyze it and find a solution for you promptly.

## How automatic API subscriptions work

<!-- block-id: intro -->

### Self-service subscriptions

Self-service plans are built for developers, data scientists, businesses, and product teams who need immediate API access to globally available, high-coverage weather data delivered through reliable, production-grade infrastructure. Our datasets provide broad geographic reach and trusted weather information used worldwide, allowing teams to build and scale independently under standard public terms.

**Included**

- Immediate online activation
- Independent subscription management
- API access under the ODbL licence
- Commercial and non-commercial use
- Technical support via our Support Centre
- Published, predictable pricing

**Licence Requirement**

- Visible attribution to OpenWeather in your application or service

**Not Included**

- Contract negotiation or customised terms
- Procurement or compliance documentation
- Dedicated account management
- Modified attribution conditions
- Enterprise service commitments

> For contract-based licensing, customised terms, or enterprise-grade usage, please see our [Enterprise Service](https://openweather.co.uk/pricing-corp).

### Self-Service Subscription Process

#### Create an Account

- [Sign up](https://openweathermap.org/home/sign_up) with your email address. Your API key is generated automatically and available in your account.

#### Choose a Plan

- Select a [subscription](https://openweathermap.org/price) based on the endpoints, usage limits, and call volume you need.

#### Subscribe online

- Complete the billing form and confirm payment.
- Your API key is activated immediately after payment.

You can view, upgrade, downgrade, or cancel your subscription at any time in your account settings.

<!-- block-id: licenses -->

### License

All automated self-service plans are provided under the ODbL (Open Database License). Commercial use is allowed.

**Standard commercial use - Attribution**

If you use OpenWeather data to power:

- Mobile apps
- Websites
- SaaS platforms
- Dashboards
- Analytics tools
- Internal business systems etc.

You only need to:

- Provide visible attribution to OpenWeather

This does **not** require you to:

- Open-source your application
- Share your product code
- Disclose your business logic

**Adapted Weather Databases - Share-Alike **

Share-alike applies only if you:

- Build a reusable dataset from OpenWeather data
- Restructure, combine, or enrich it
- Operate your own weather dataset or API based on stored OpenWeather data
- Make that dataset or API available outside your organisation

If the result remains fundamentally weather data derived from OpenWeather, the nature of the data has not changed.

If such a database is distributed externally, it must be offered under the same ODbL license.

<!-- block-id: license_enterprise -->

> In most commercial use cases, you only need to provide **attribution** on the screen or page where weather data appears.
>
> Attribution placed only in hidden documentation or deep legal pages is not sufficient.
>
> **Recommended line:**
>
> Weather data © OpenWeather
>

# How to start working with OpenWeather APIs

**OpenWeather delivers reliable, global weather data through structured APIs designed for straightforward integration. Access current conditions, forecasts, historical archives, and specialised datasets to support applications ranging from lightweight services to large-scale operational systems.**

<!-- block-id: openweather_api_overview -->

## OpenWeather APIs overview

OpenWeather provides reliable, global weather data through structured, industry-standard APIs.

Our services support a wide range of applications, from lightweight integrations to large-scale data systems, delivering current conditions, forecasts, historical weather, and specialised datasets.

Access is immediate. Integration is straightforward. Pricing is transparent.

- [View pricing & subscribe](/price.md)

<!-- block-id: data_available -->

## What data is available

OpenWeather APIs provide:

- Current weather conditions
- Minute-by-minute forecasts
- Hourly and daily forecasts
- Short-term and extended outlooks
- Government weather alerts
- 47+ years of historical observations
- Historical forecast archives
- Statistical climate data
- Air quality data
- Weather maps and geospatial layers
- Industry-focused APIs (Solar, Road Risk, Agromonitoring, and others)

Coverage is global, data is available for any coordinate worldwide.

All services are delivered via REST APIs with structured JSON responses suitable for integration into web, mobile, analytics, IoT, and enterprise environments.

- [Documentation](/api.md)

<!-- block-id: products -->

## Core API products

**One Call API 4.0**. A comprehensive weather endpoint for a specific location, combining current, forecast, historical data, and alerts within a single API call.

**Forecast & Current Weather APIs**. Short-term and extended forecasts with frequent updates.

**Historical Weather APIs**. 47+ years of hourly archive data, forecast history, and statistical datasets.

**Weather Maps & Geospatial APIs**. Layer-based weather maps, precipitation data, and visual datasets.

Detailed API documentation and integration guidance are available for all products.

- [Documentation](/api.md)

<!-- block-id: technology_accuracy -->

## Technology and data quality

OpenWeather OWHL™ model operates with:

- Ground weather stations and sensors
- Satellite systems
- Radar networks
- Global forecast models including GFS and ECMWF

Data updates are released every 10 minutes to ensure timely delivery.

Short-term forecasts demonstrate strong predictive performance. As with all atmospheric modelling, forecast uncertainty increases over longer time horizons.

Continuous model refinement and real-time data processing ensure consistent global coverage across both urban and remote regions.

- [Technology](https://openweather.co.uk/technology)
- [Accuracy](/accuracy-and-quality.md)

## How to start using Weather API

Getting started requires only a few steps:

1. Create an OpenWeather [account](https://home.openweathermap.org/users/sign_in)
2. Select the API product appropriate for your needs on the [APIs page](https://openweathermap.org/api)
3. Choose a subscription plan on the [Pricing](https://openweathermap.org/price) page
4. Receive your API key instantly (no approval or onboarding process required)
5. Integrate using the provided [documentation](https://openweathermap.org/api)

[Free](https://openweathermap.org/price) plans are available for evaluation and development.

[Paid plans](/price.md) scale according to usage.

- [Select plan and subscribe](/price.md)

<!-- block-id: licensing -->

## Licensing

OpenWeather self-service products are provided under the **Open Database License (ODbL)** framework. You may use the data to build applications, websites, dashboards, analytics tools, and commercial products.

The key difference under ODbL is **whether your product is only showing results** from OpenWeather data, or whether you are **building a new dataset/API where the data is still essentially weather data derived from OpenWeather**.

In other words: **the “nature” of the data matters**.

1) Displaying weather in your app or service (Produced Work)

If you use OpenWeather data to show weather information to end users, for example in an app, website, dashboard, or report,  you are producing a **Produced Work**.

In this case, you are presenting outputs (maps, charts, forecasts, insights), not providing a database to others.

**Main requirement:** attribution to OpenWeather.

2) Building a weather dataset or API where the data is still “weather data” (Adapted Database)

If you store, restructure, combine, or enrich OpenWeather data and the result is still fundamentally **weather data derived from OpenWeather**, even if delivered through your own dataset, feed, or API, this may be considered an **Adapted Database**.

Examples include:

- Storing large volumes of OpenWeather data as a reusable dataset
- Restructuring the data into your own schema or database
- Combining OpenWeather data with other data and keeping it as a structured dataset
- Creating a weather API or data service backed by stored OpenWeather-derived data

**Important:** changing the format, schema, or adding calculations does not remove the origin of the data. If it still functions as weather data derived from OpenWeather, Adapted Database rules may apply.

If that adapted database (or a service giving access to it) is made available **outside your organisation**, **share-alike conditions apply** meaning the adapted database must be offered under the same ODbL terms.

- [License](https://openweathermap.org/full-price#licenses)

## Academic Initiatives

OpenWeather supports academic and research communities via non-profit [Weather Foundation](https://weatherfoundation.org). Universities, research institutions, professors, and students can use OpenWeather data for:

- Scientific research
- Climate studies
- Environmental modelling
- Urban planning research
- Academic publications
- Student projects and theses

Weather data plays a critical role in global research, and we believe it should be accessible for scientific progress.

Academic usage is typically supported through:

- Special academic access options
- Educational discounts or dedicated plans (where applicable)
- Clear licensing under the open data framework

For larger institutional research projects, data redistribution, or long-term structured datasets, Enterprise arrangements may be required.

- [Explore free data and initiatives](https://weatherfoundation.org)

# Historical Weather Data: Formats, APIs, and Bulk Downloads

Explore the different ways to access historical weather data with OpenWeather — from bulk archives to API queries for any timestamp. This guide helps you choose the best option depending on your use case, data volume, and level of detail.

## What historical weather data OpenWeather provides

OpenWeather provides several types of historical weather data designed for different use cases — from long-term climate analysis to retrieving weather conditions for a specific moment in the past.

Depending on your needs, you can access historical data in several formats:

- Bulk downloadable archives covering many years
- Historical forecasts (past model outputs)
- API access to weather data for any past timestamp
- Aggregated daily historical statistics
- Timeline endpoints combining historical and forecast data

### History Bulks

Downloadable datasets in CSV and JSON formats

Time Coverage: 47+ years back (from January 01, 1979)

Geo coverage: Worldwide

Access Method: Downloadable datasets

Available through our [Marketplace](https://home.openweathermap.org/marketplace)

### History Forecast Bulks

Downloadable Historical archive of 16-days forecast weather data, CSV and JSON formats

Time Coverage: 8+ years back (from October 7, 2017)

Geo coverage: Worldwide

Access Method: Downloadable datasets

Available through our [Marketplace](https://home.openweathermap.org/marketplace)

### Historical weather via One Call 4.0

Historical weather via One Call 4.0 for any timestamp

Time Coverage: 47+ years back (from January 01, 1979)

Geo coverage: Worldwide

Access Method: API via One Call API 4.0

### Daily aggregated history

Daily aggregated historical weather via One Call 4.0

Time Coverage: 47+ years back (from January 01, 1979)

Geo coverage: Worldwide

Access Method: API via One Call API 4.0

### Statistical Weather API

Statistical data on main weather parameters for any day and month of the year

The statistics are calculated based on our [Historical weather data](https://openweathermap.org/history)

JSON format

The weather data updated every hour

Statistical Weather Data API is available in Expert subscription plan

## Historical data access methods

**1️⃣ Downloadable historical datasets**

Large downloadable archives covering multiple years of historical weather observations and model data.
Includes:

- History Bulks
- History Forecast Bulks

Best for: Machine learning, climate research, long-term analytics.
Available through our [Marketplace](https://home.openweathermap.org/marketplace)

**2️⃣ Historical weather via API**

Retrieve historical weather conditions for specific locations and timestamps via API.
Includes:

- One Call 4.0 Historical endpoint
- Daily aggregated history

Best for: Analytical Dashboards, on-demand queries.
Available via [One Call API 4.0 subscription](/price.md#one_call) or [Professional subscriptions](/full-price.md).

# One Call API 2.5 Deprecated

One Call API 2.5 has been deprecated in June 2024. We advise you to switch to [One Call API 3.0](/api/one-call-3.md) and prepared the [detailed guide](/one-call-transfer.md) for transitioning.

## About One Call API 3.0

As opposed to our subscriptions with fixed monthly cost, [One Call API 3.0](/api/one-call-3.md) has its own, separate subscription that has a variable cost, in proportion to your actual use of the API. Apart from additional functionality (47+ years of historical data are now available via this API), users can configure and limit their usage to ensure that they don’t make more request than expected. Read more about this subscription plan in the [FAQ](/faq.md#onecall).

Here are the types of data that are available:

- [**Current weather and forecasts:**](/api/one-call-3.md#current)
and government weather alerts
- - minute forecast for 1 hour
  - hourly forecast for 48 hours
  - daily forecast for 8 days
- [**Weather data for any timestamp**](/api/one-call-3.md#history) for 47+ years historical archive and 4 days ahead forecast
- [**Daily aggregation**](/api/one-call-3.md#history_daily_aggregation) of weather data for 47+ years archive and 1.5 years ahead forecast
- [**Weather overview**](/api/one-call-3.md#weather_overview) with a human-readable weather summary for today and tomorrow's forecast, utilizing OpenWeather AI technologies

## Pay as you call

1,000 API calls per day for free

**0.0012 GBP** per API call over the daily limit

- [Subscribe to One Call by Call](https://home.openweathermap.org/subscriptions/unauth_subscribe/onecall_30/base)

If you have any questions, please fell free to [contact us](https://home.openweathermap.org/questions).

### History bulk

Download up to 47+ years back historical weather data for any location worldwide.

Key features:

- Data available from January 1, 1979
- Global coverage (any coordinates)
- Hourly data resolution
- Available in CSV and JSON formats

Ideal for long-term analysis, climate research, modelling, and data-driven forecasting.

### History forecast bulk

Access archived 16-day forecasts exactly as they were issued for any location worldwide.

Key features:

- Data available from October 7, 2017
- Global coverage (any coordinates)
- Archive of previously generated 16-day forecasts
- Available in CSV and JSON formats

Ideal for forecast verification, model validation, and performance analysis.

### Global Precipitation Maps (history and forecast)

Radar-based maps providing highly precise precipitation data for any location worldwide.

Key features:

- Global coverage
- Current precipitation data
- Short-term forecast:
- - Up to 6 hours for the US
  - Up to 2 hours for other regions
- Historical data: last 2 days with 10-minute frequency
- Designed for real-time monitoring and high-resolution visualization

Ideal for flood monitoring, transport operations, outdoor planning, and weather-sensitive decision-making.

### Weather Maps 2.0 1-hour

Access hourly updated global weather map layers for visualization and monitoring applications.

Key features:

- Hourly forecast map layers
- Parameters including temperature, precipitation, clouds, pressure, wind, and more
- Global coverage
- Tile-based map format for easy integration
- Designed for web and mobile weather map visualization

Ideal for building interactive weather maps, dashboards, and geospatial monitoring tools.

### Solar Irradiance API

Access real-time and forecasted solar irradiance data for any location worldwide.

Key features:

- Current and 16-day solar irradiance forecasts
- GHI, DNI, and DHI indices
- Clear-sky and cloudy-sky models
- Global coverage by geographic coordinates
- Pay-as-you-call
- Delivered via API in JSON format

Ideal for solar energy monitoring, system optimization, and performance forecasting.

### Solar Panel Energy Prediction

Estimate solar power generation and panel performance for any location worldwide using advanced weather and irradiance models.

Key features:

- Solar energy production forecasts based on panel configuration
- Support for tilt angle, orientation, and system parameters
- Current conditions and forecast-based energy output
- Global coverage by geographic coordinates
- Delivered via API in JSON format

Ideal for solar project planning, system optimization, and performance forecasting.

### Wind service

Accurate wind speed and direction data for any location worldwide, available for hub heights between 10 and 500 meters.

Key features:

- Wind data at custom heights (10–500 m)
- Current conditions and 16-day forecasts
- High-resolution time steps (hourly or 15-minute)
- Global coverage by coordinates
- Flexible delivery options (API, bulk, S3, FTP, dashboard)

Ideal for wind energy assessment, turbine optimization, and wind-sensitive operations.

### Solar Irradiance History Bulk

Download 47+ years of historical solar irradiance data for any location worldwide via bulk access.

Key features:

- Data available for 47+ years back
- 15-minute and 1-hour resolution
- GHI, DNI, DHI indices
- Clear-sky and cloudy-sky models
- Available by geographic point (lat/lon coordinates)

Ideal for solar energy modelling, performance assessment, and long-term resource analysis.

### Solar Irradiance History Forecast Bulk

Download an archive of previously generated 16-day solar irradiance forecasts for any location worldwide.

Key features:

- Historical forecasts available from April 2017 onward
- 16-day forecast archive with 1-hour resolution (15-minute step available on request)
- Includes clear-sky and cloudy-sky solar irradiance forecasts
- Global coverage by coordinates
- Exportable in CSV and JSON formats

Access to the full archive by request

### Road Risk API

Access real-time and forecasted road weather risk data for any location worldwide to support safer and more efficient transport operations.

Key features:

- Current and forecast road risk conditions
- Risk indicators based on weather parameters (e.g., temperature, precipitation, wind, visibility, national alerts, etc.)
- Global coverage by geographic coordinates
- Designed for route planning and fleet management systems
- Delivered via API in JSON format

Ideal for logistics, fleet operators, navigation platforms, and weather-sensitive transportation services.

### Fire Weather Index

Advanced fire danger assessment data to support wildfire prevention, monitoring, and risk management.

Key features:

- Fire risk index based on weather conditions
- Current data and forecast availability
- High-resolution coverage by geographic coordinates
- Designed for environmental monitoring and emergency planning
- Delivered via [Index API](/api/fire-index-api.md) and [Fire Weather Index Maps](/api/fire-index-map.md)

Ideal for forestry services, environmental agencies, insurers, and risk management platforms.

### AgroMonitoring

A professional agricultural intelligence platform delivering satellite-based crop and field monitoring data worldwide.

Key features:

- Vegetation indices (NDVI, EVI, NDWI, DSWI, NRI, and more)
- Soil temperature and soil moisture data
- Weather-based agricultural insights
- Historical and forecast data integration
- Field-level monitoring by polygon or coordinates

Ideal for precision agriculture, farm management, agribusiness analytics, and yield optimization.

For organisations that require more than standard self-service access, OpenWeather Enterprise provides a contract-based service with broader licensing, procurement support, tailored commercial terms, and enterprise-grade delivery.

# Support centre

OpenWeather’s support centre is not only a team of specialists ready to help you with any issue but also a set of tools and resources designed to make it easier for you to use our services. Whether you are just starting out with APIs, an experienced developer, or a business, our team is ready to provide answers to your questions.

## OpenWeather AI assistant Ulla

Ulla, the OpenWeather AI assistant, is an AI-powered tool trained on our products and services to provide seamless support. Whether you are exploring APIs, troubleshooting issues, or seeking guidance, Ulla is designed to aid you in navigating OpenWeather's product offerings.

What is Ulla: it is the advanced AI technology powering the OpenWeather assistant. Originally developed as a corporate AI assistant, Ulla specialises in transcriptions, summaries, and secure data management, supporting business across industries with innovative solutions. Explore more at [ulla.bot](https://ulla.bot/).

Ulla is just starting out in beta and may make some mistakes. Consider checking important information. We are working to improve and develop the assistant to give the most accurate answers. Let us know if you notice any mistakes, and we will correct it.

FAQ is a collection with a detailed information about most popular topics

- Payment Processing including Information about security measures in place to protect payment information.
- Troubleshooting Payment Issues: Helpful tips for resolving common payment problems you may encounter.

- Types of Products and Data Included: Comprehensive details on the various APIs available.

The "Personal Account" chapter aims to assist users in understanding and managing their personal accounts effectively. This chapter covers topics related to account management, and troubleshooting, ensuring users can quickly find the information they need. Key areas include:

### API errors

For each error code, we provide a clear explanation of what it means and how it relates to your request or operation and describe common reasons why errors might occur, such as incorrect parameters, authentication failures, or connectivity issues. This information is designed to help you identify the issue quickly and take appropriate action.

# Weather Triggers

> The Weather Triggers API has been deprecated on 2025.
>
> If you are seeking functionality related to weather-based triggers, we recommend using the [OpenWeather Dashboard](https://dashboard.openweather.co.uk/), which provides a wide range of tools and customizable features for monitoring weather conditions.
>
> For those looking to implement similar functionality via API, we suggest exploring the [OpenWeather Alerts product](https://openweather.co.uk/products/openweather-alerts). This service offers robust and flexible alerting capabilities designed to meet a variety of use cases.
>
> If you require a custom solution or have specific integration needs, please don’t hesitate to contact our [Support team](mailto:info@openweathermap.org).
